text:
This is a wonderful recipe.  Please don't be deterred by the "extra preparation" noted in some of the reviews.  Every step is worth it, from browning the meat to deglazing the pan.  This hearty and flavorful stew satisfied my family and dinner guests.  Everyone went back for more.

I followed the recipe as written, using merlot for the red wine because I like the rich flavor and Yukon Gold potatoes because I like their taste and texture and they were on hand for the Potato Fougasse (potato bread with olive oil and rosemary) I made to accompany the stew.  They were wonderful together.  Trust your instincts when thickening the stew once it is done.  Some reviews complained about consistency but you really need to decide what it needs for yourself using more or less of a flour/water paste than indicated.  Do what works for you.  (And by the way, if you have extra merlot use it with the flour instead of water to thicken the stew to impart some extra flavor.)

text:
Yum! This is a great basic recipe  but I did make some changes. I marinated the beef in the wine and some minced garlic for a few hours (I made this on a weekend). I floured and fried in oil as directed. I omitted the onion soup and we didn't miss it at all, but I did use beef broth in place of the water. I added celery and mushrooms, and also tossed some peas in at the very end.  I added a bay leaf and some thyme and a pinch of rosemary. Next time, I might add some tomato paste or diced tomatoes. Very tasty and hearty.

text:
This was REALLY good...the meat was kind of dry but that might be user error ... :)  I'll still give it a 5. (of course my house still smells like stew...)

I used about 1.25# of meat or so, Lipton beefy onion soup mix, 2 small packs of baby carrots, 2 red potatoes, and 1 onion.  I didn't saute the onions in butter either.  I prepped this the night before, and next morning, popped it in the crock pot.  It cooked on low for 12 hrs (might account for the dryness).  The meat shredded easily.  My fiance thought it was tasty, so I think this recipe is a keeper.  I might add some beef broth next time for more liquid to combat the dryness.  The pepper really gives it a little kick!  I didn't have to thicken the gravy because I had dumped in the flour from the meat.

All in all, a successful first crock pot experience... :)

                    *note - I've made this several times now, and adding the can of beef broth really helps!  From now on, I'll make sure all of my crock pot dishes have enough liquid to cover the meat!  I also have been using sweet potatoes in lieu of regular potatoes...yum!

5 stars with my revisions.  I made this for the first time and it was amazing.  I also halved the recipe.  Its just me and my hubby.  To the initial bag of flour I did add some fresh ground black pepper while shaking up the beef to coat with flour and pepper.  I used 2 carrots and 2 celery stalks and 1 can diced tomatoes.  I did add a chicken and a beef bouillion cube to the boiling water as well as the Onion Soup Mix.  And I increased the boiling water mixture by 1/4 c so that I could use it at the end to make the flour mixture to thicken the stew.  I sauted 1 medium onion and 3 garlic cloves and then added that to the bottom of the crockpot.  I also browned the meat and then removed it from the pan and then used about 1/2c of red wine (Pinot Noir) to scrape up the brown bits using my wooden spoon.  I didnt use any butter, only used Olive Oil.  To the crockpot I did add 1/2t of Paprika, 1t of Worcesetershire sauce and a couple of shakes of salt, way less then 1/2t.  I poured the wine brown bits into the crock pot.  I placed it on hi and it was ready to eat in 3 1/2hours. My God, this was so amazing.  I was in heaven, so was my hubby and it disappeared!  We ate this for 3 days straight, lunch and dinner and had double servings.  OMG, thanks for posting a great basic recipe that turned out fantastic to our tastes.

text:
I did have to tweak this recipe a bit, but I still believe it's worthy of a five star rating. I could never make a stew without adding some garlic, and so 5 minced cloves went into the crock pot. I also added some celery chunks and replaced the water with a hearty red wine. Super delicious, warming and hearty!

And please remember, you don't have to follow recipes to a T. If you have a little cooking experience under your belt, then use your own instincts to make these recipes yours. For instance, some reviewers gave a lower rating to this recipe because they thickened the stew too much. But that's completely avoidable. Simply add the water/flour mixture slowly, stir and see how thick it gets. If it's thick enough before you use it all up, stop. You're done. Oh, and using red wine in place of the water for thickening will give a deep, layered flavor to your stew this is fabulous. If you don't like cooking with wine, then I would advise using beef broth in place of the water in this recipe.

This is the best stew I have ever eaten! Everyone in the family loves when I make it.  I only change a couple things. Instead of using a bag to mix the beef and flour mixture in, I find it easier to use a medium container with lid. It coats more evenly and is a bit less messy. Yes, it sounds like a bit much wine, but it adds wonderful flavor (I use Merlot).

text:
Good stew! While I enjoyed this quite a bit, I still prefer the stew recipe from my "Fix it & Forget It" cookbook that I stumbled upon years ago. This recipe is really just a pot roast in stew form. The next time I make this, I'd do just that - skip the stew meat and instead add a large roast to my slow cooker (or set the expectation up front and call this "pot roast stew"). I'd also bulk up on the carrots (love em!), add some celery and serve over egg noodles to sop up the yummy gravy. I pretty much followed IAMROSIE's directions to the letter except for subbing beef broth for the water added to the corstarch mixture (I had just enough for that but not enough to sub for the boiling water added to the onion soup mix) and using beefy onion mix instead of plain 'ol onion soup mix (again, because I didn't have enough broth to sub for the H2O called for). I also peeled my potatoes (personal preference). My wine of choice was merlot. I cooked everything exactly as directed with excellent results. NOTE: Don't let the cornstarch mixture fool you.... I thought it would be a slurry (i.e. watery), but it turned out to be a very thick paste. Once added to my slow cooker, it dissolved and worked its magic! :) Served with J.P.'s big daddy's biscuits and simple baked apples for dessert (two recipes on this site), this was a nice fall meal. Thanks for sharing, IAMROSIE! :-)

text:
Wow!  We love, love, LOVE this beef stew!  We made some modification based on what other reviewers had said, and the final product was amazing.  We browned the flour and salt, plus 1/2tsp. paprika and garlic covered meat, then put it in the crockpot.  In the same pan as the meat, I browned the onions until soft, then added 4 Tbsp. minced garlic, waited until it was fragrant, and then turned off the heat and added 3/4 of wine, making sure to scrape all the browned bits up. Then I put that mixture in the crockpot. I added the carrots, parsley, pepper, and onion soup like the recipe called for, and exchanged the water for beef broth, and added 1 tsp. Worcestershire sauce, 1/2 tsp. Paprika, 2 Bay leafs, 1 tsp. thyme and rosemary.  I omitted the potatoes, and served it over egg noddles.  

This made for an amazing stew!  Can't wait to make it again!

text:
Wonderful recipe - this is a keeper! Took a little longer than 15 minutes for the prep (unless all your vegies/potatoes are pre-cut), so maybe expect more like 30 minutes for the prep. I followed the recipe pretty closely except for liberally adding a few teaspoons of garlic (crushed - the fresh garlic that comes in a jar) and making the liquid half bordeaux wine and half water. Loved the flavor and aroma the wine added, but next time I will probably use beef stock instead of the water and maybe add some Worcestershire sauce to give it a more robust beefy taste - and make the total liquid added to the slow cooker equal about a cup more than specified in the recipe. I wouldn't be shy about adding a few more spices - like rosemary, fresh ground black pepper, etc. to taste. I don't like the idea of the MSG in the onion soup mix, but I would not leave the onion soup mix out - this recipe benefits tremendously from its taste. I think it would definitely be missing something significant without it. I cooked mine overnight because I work very long days (11-hours) so cooking it through the day was not an option. I cooked it on high for about 1.5 hours and turned it down to low for another 5 hours. It came out with the vegies maybe just a touch too al-dente. I might consider adding another hour cooking at low next time. I didn't thicken the liquid at the end - it didn't need it. The meat turned out very tender and moist. Keep the size of potatoes and vegies small and bite-sized.

I thought this was a pretty simple and hearty stew. I added some celery, about 1 cup also some garlic about 2 cloves. I didnt thicken it up at the end because I used russet potatos and they seemed to do the job. I made dumplings to go with it instead of bread or buns. All of the ingredients didnt fit inside my crock pot, and I have a fairly huge one. So what I did was used a roasting pan and set the oven to 350F and cooked the stew for 1 hour before turning the oven down to 200F. I let the stew cook for 5 hours stiring once in a while. It turned out great and the meat was tender and falling apart. I will make this again for sure!

text:
This is the best beef stew I have ever had. Don't be discouraged by the extra prep time. It is completely worth it. I've made this stew at least 10 times and have changed a few things. I just use a big bowl to coat the meat in flour and salt. It seems a little easier than messing around with a bag. I also only use one large onion and one head of celery (instead of 3 onions). I tried substituting the red wine with red wine vinegar once and I think it's better with red wine. I cook the entire 12 servings for just my husband and I. It's worth it, it feeds us for days!

text:
Base recipe is the perfect stating point for making it your own. The modifications I have made are as follows.
I used a 2 lb london broil cut into 1/2-3/4" squares and added a can of Cambells Golden Mushroom soup to the 2-cups of boiling water. I also cut the potatoes into 1/2-3/4" pieces and sliced to carrots to about a 1/4" thick. I also added 1-cup of frozen peas. The Golden mushroom soup will thicken it to the point that you won't need the 2-tablespoons of flour in step 4. I've cooked this four times (including today) and the family loves it!

text:
The basic recipe was the formula for a better beef stew.  I made the following modifications-

- Added four tablespoons of worcestershire sauce
- Added celery stalks, cut down into 3" stalks
- Added about a 1.5 cups of early peas, ON TOP of the stew to keep the peas from getting crushed, in the last fifteen minutes of cooking.
- Used two tablespoons of garlic salt, and two tablespoons of lemon pepper with the flour for coating the beef.
- Used Dutch mini potatoes- Cut the oversized ones in half place and place at the bottom of the crockpot.
- Used Vidalia (sweet onions), cut in quarters, peeled and then then hand separated for sauteeing purposes
- Used 1/2 cup of Burgundy wine and a tablespoom of minced garlic to marinate the meat, overnight.
- Cut back on the stewing beef used to only 2 pounds
- Used a packet of Swansons beef base sauce
- Went a little extra heavy on the veggies

text:
Great recipe to start with! However, you'll have to "tweek" them to suit your taste buds. My changes: Seasoned the meat with garlic powder, black pepper and adobo then marinaded in 1 cups of Worcestershire & 1/4-1/2 cup hot pepper sauce combo min. 8 hrs (the longer the better). I also poured the marinade in the crock pot with approx. 1 1/2 to 2 cup of red wine and 1 cup of beef broth. I omitted using plain water in lieu of wine. I found that its best to use enough liquid to at least cover the meat. 2 bay leaves, 3 red potatoes, 2 sweet potatoes, 3 celery stalks, 3-5 carrots, 1 spanish onion, 1 1/2 of chopped garlic, 1-2 Tblsp fresh thyme, 1-2 Tblsp fresh rosemary, 2 bay leaves. I omitted the onion soup. The quantity of veggies depends on the size of your pot. I DID brown the stew beef as directed. Next time I will saute the garlic and onions to soften. Lastly, the amount of warm water and flour "slurry mix"  you'll need will depend on how much "juice" you have. I strongly recommend checking near end of your cooking time. I added a little at a time then thicken to the way I wanted it. BTW the second day the stew was even better! The Worcestershire and fresh herbs brought the dish together!

text:
I'm a novice at slow cooking and I have to say this is the best beef stew I have ever tasted. I changed it quite a bit to suit my tastes, and used the recipe for the basic guidelines on how to prepare it, cooking times, and liquid amounts. I substituted the onion soup mix with garlic powder, dried chopped onions, and used beef stock instead of water. I also used olive oil instead of butter when I sauteed the onions, and added 1 tablespoon of paprika. I prefer London Broil instead of stew meat. I like the tenderness and the reduced fat. It saves prep time. Overall, great recipe!!  Additional Items Added:  3 cloves of garlic 1 tbs of paprika 1 cup of mushrooms 1/2 can of peas 1/2 can of corn 1 can of diced tomatoes with juice extra carrots (large not baby) Beef stock instead of water Homemade Onion Mix instead of store bought (I didn't want added sodium) London Broil instead of stew meat

We just tried this stew last week after my husband found it and requested it. Since I was running short on time, I took another reviewer's advice and put it on high for 1 1/2 hours and low for another 3 hours. The carrots were still hard so we cranked it back on high for another 30 minutes. Next time, I am going to try it with the regular timing. The flavor and consistency of the stew was perfect. I also used a full bag of baby carrots and a bit more potato than the recipe called for and it was not a problem. The only other thing I would mention is that the prep time is a "crock"...excuse the pun... 15 minutes is laughable... More like 45 min- 1 hour. Otherwise, a very delicious stew recipe. I will certainly make it again.

text:
OK starting point but needs more flavor.  More spices are needed and more flavorful vegetables.

Here's my recommendations:

Change meat from 3 lbs to 2 lbs

Change 3 large potatoes to 2 large white potatoes + 1 large sweet potato or yam

Change the cup of baby carrots to 3-4 carrots cut into large pieces (baby carrots DO NOT have the same depth of flavor)

Change the two cups boiling water to two cups beef broth

Add 1 small can of baby peas at the end of the cooking time while the gravy is thickening

Add the following seasonings:

2 Bay Leaves
2 TB Worcestershire Sauce
2 tsp Garlic Powder
1 tsp Paprika
2 tsp Salt

It's definitely a keeper with these changes.

My boyfriend and I really enjoyed this dish.  I did make a few alterations to suit our preferences.  I added half of a package of ranch dip mix to give it a bit more flavor.  I also added 3 stalks of celery and a seeded and halved habanero pepper to give it a bite;  I removed each half when the stew was finished. My wife and I knew we where going to have a long day coming up, so I was looking for a slow cooker meal. My wife really loves carrots, so I put in a full pound. I love the potatoes, so I added extras. We both love the liquids, so I doubled the water and dry soup mix. I did not have red wine on hand , so I skipped that step. I completed steps one through three the night before and place everything in the refrigerator. The next morning I placed the slow cooker on the counter set at low heat. Thirteen hours later I completed the last two tasks of step four. This was awesomely delicious. The stew meat nearly melted in your mouth. The potatoes and carrots were perfectly tender and flavorful. We will definitely make this again and again.

text:
I cut the meat down to 2lbs, and thought the ratio was good.  I recommend seasoning the meat before flour to ensure balance.  I use a salt/pepper/garlic powder blend (Paula Dean house seasoning).  I did use a can beef broth instead of water to mix with onion soup.  Deglazing is kind of a wasted step when you use non-stick pans (I know, "THE HUMANITY").  I still did it because I wanted the wine.  3 onions seem excessive to me, so I used 1 really big one.  You can really eyeball potatoes and carrots to get the perfect mix that works for you.  I was a little surprised that no one expressed concern that there wasn't enough liquid when you firt put everything in.  Don't worry, just step away from the pot and it will take care of itself.  I don't know why anyone would need to thicken this stew up.  If you have enough potatoes (we're potato people), the starch from the potatoes breaking down should thicken this up very nicely.  I even added 1/4 of wine toward the end to thin, and to give it that extra kick of flavor.  This really isn't as much of a change as it looks.

Oh My! This was delish!!! 
I made a few very small changes though.  I added maybe a just the smallest splash more of wine than said, okay okay, I used a half of a cup  :).... I used a whole bag of baby carrots and used baby red potatoes, quartered instead of 4 large russets.  I also added about a teaspoon of minced garlic.  I used a can of beef broth mixed with the onion soup, which measured to about a cup and a half and used water to get the required 2 cups.  I cooked it on low for 6 hours, never did the high part nor the addition of flour at the end because it was thick enough.  In the last 30 minutes I added about 2 cups of frozen green peas because I just like peas in my stew. :)  
My guests said that it was probably some of the best beef stew that they have ever eaten.  Sounds about right to me!  Yummay!

text:
REALLY great recipe ... I tried to make it a bit easier on myself by browning the meat the day before and putting it in the frig overnight; also peeled and chopped the potatoes and put them in a gallon ziplock baggie, covered in water with a tsp of lemon juice added, in the frig overnight (the lemon juice keeps the potatoes from turning brown; be sure to drain and rinse well before putting into the stew). Then in the morning I sauteed my onion (used only one, large, onion) and added all ingredients together into the crockpot. Took another reviewers' suggestion of using wine in place of the water, combined with the flour at the end to thicken.  My son ate his with a fork it was so thick! Simply delicious, and worth the time!!!

text:
WOW!  This stew turned out amazing!  So flavorful, and the meat just fell apart!  Adding the flour and water at the end as stated in the recipe gave it just the right thickness for us.  Let me caution other cooking novices like myself.  The preparation time of 15 minutes is assuming your meat/potatoes are already cubed, onions already sliced, etc.  I didn't have any of that done ahead of time (I did have to cube my meat myself and chop fresh parsley) and prep took nearly an hour.  I do wonder what the result would be if I just threw all the ingredients into the crock without the extra prep....but most other reviewers agree that the extra prep is what makes the difference in this recipe.  It is DELISH!

I hate when I read a review and the writer states the many changes that were made. However, I made a couple of changes myself. I used beef broth instead of water and added mushrooms. This stew if very yummy. I agree with another reviewer, it should be called Beef Pot Roast Stew. I love the flavors and will make this again with a few more changes. I'd at least double the wine (I use Burgandy for full flavor) and add another 1/2 can of broth. I'd also chop the carrots into smaller pieces. The reason I gave it 4 stars is because it needed the broth versus the water. It would have been too bland without it. While this is a great recipe that I'll make again, it still isn't what I am looking for in a beef stew.

text:
Best beef stew I have ever had/made!  It was snowing and VERY cold in Kansas City this weekend, so this was the perfect thing to make!  I changed a few things, which only made this recipe sooooo much better.  I used almost 4 lbs of meat, which I marinated in red wine and garlic overnight.  In the morning, I threw it all together.  I used beef broth instead of water and I sauteed a whole bunch of mushrooms with my onions.  I did not have the need to deglaze the skillet.  Once everything was in the crock pot, I added an entire can of tomato paste.  After the 6 or so hours, I added frozen peas and two envelopes of dry brown gravy mix.  It could NOT have been more perfect!  This is now THE recipe for beef stew; I will be making this again and again.

Tasty.  Made a few changes, as I always do.  Use 2 lbs of meat instead of 3, 3/4 cup merlot instead of a 1/4 c), added 1 packet Montreal Steak seasoning some to the the flour and the rest to the stew itself (if you add this.. you can eliminate the pepper).  I also added a few shots of worcestershire sauce and 2 bay leaves.  Oh, I also only used the powder from the onion soup mix not the dried onions (use the beefy onion soup mix, gives it a little extra beef flavor). Threw it in crock pot for 8 hours, yummy!!!  Thanks Rosie!!!

text:
I just made this for the first time. I did not have wine, but I improvised with 50/50 Southern Comfort and boiling water (I would not go out of my way for this, but it was in the house and no one was drinking it) and added 3 stalks of celery, because, well, I'm Irish and love celery in stew. Don't add more liquid if you think there is not enough, just stir it up a bit. Juices will come out of the fats in the beef in time. Cooked on high 45 min and low 4.5 hours, could have gone a little longer to reduce the broth to a stewy consistency but I could not wait any longer! My house smells awesome and this filling stew will be made again!

I made several changes for this recipe.  I didn't include 2 cups of boiling water or dry onion soup mix.  Neither did I use 1/4 cup of warm water.  I subsituted 8 small Yukon Gold potatoes for 4 large cubed potatoes.  I added, thyme, crushed red pepper, 28 oz. beef broth, salt, basil (dried), 2 bay leaves, 1 1/2 cups Merlot wine, 5 crushed garlic cloves and 2 celery ribs and worchestershire sauce.  I also used 2 lbs ox-tail instead of 3 lbs of beef stew meat.
I failed to use the drippings from browning the ox-tails in a skillet.  I also didn't thicken the stew with flour.  What resulted was a flavorful ox-tail stew with a tad bit of spicyness.  A thoroughly delicious stew and not bland whatsoever !!

text:
This recipe is DELICIOUS! Thank you IAMROSIE for posting it! I have tried several other beef stew recipes from this website, and this is by far my favorite. While other stew recipes can be bland, this one has excellent flavor. For the dry onion soup mix I used this recipe: http://allrecipes.com/Recipe/Dry-Onion-Soup-Mix/Detail.aspx?event8=1&prop24=SR_Thumb&e11=dry%20onion%20soup&e8=Quick%20Search&event10=1&e7=Home%20Page&soid=sr_results_p1i1.

I was hesitant to use three onions in the recipe, since it already calls for dry onion soup mix, but three is definitely the right amount. Additionally, I added the flour 20 minutes before serving in order to get the right consistency.

I would not change anything about this recipe, it is perfect. My girlfriend loves this recipe, too, and she doesn't normally eat meat. This is a restaurant quality beef stew, or better.

text:
I really liked this stew. Great flavor, very rich and thick. I had to make a few changes, however. First, 3 pounds of meat was too much. Maybe the recipe used a much larger slow cooker than mine. I used about 2 pounds of meat. 

Also, it was a little too thick and not enough sauce. When it was almost ready, I actually removed at least a 1/3 of the ingredients (meat, potatoes, and carrots), leaving 2/3 of the recipe and the sauce in the slow cooker. I then added the 1/4 cup water and 2 tbs flour so the sauce could thicken. At that point, it was a nearly perfect stew. I added a bit more salt (to taste) and just a bit more red wine, let it sit for about 5 minutes and then served.

Everyone loved it!

As to the 1/3 of the ingredients that were removed from the recipe, after our dinner, I just put them all back in the slow cooker, which of course left very little of the sauce, but it was still a great lunch the next day.

text:
This was a great recipe and I didn't have to tweak the seasonings like I typically do! I did everything in the crockpot (because I'm lazy like that) and loved how this came out. To start with, I put the beef in the crock pot and added about 3 TBS of flour directly to the pot and stirred it together with the meat, then threw in the remaining called for ingredients including the diced onion (skipped the butter and skipped browning the onions). I added hot water, not boiling and I didn't have red wine so I used beef broth instead. I used half white and half sweet potatoes and tossed in some leftover mushrooms I had as well. I set it on low and it was tender and delicious 8 hours later! This is a great crockpot beef stew recipe that I will gladly use again!

text:
I tweeked this a bit: added 1/2 tsp paprika, tsp of graymaster darkener, 1tsp of worcestshire sauce, 1/2 tsp cumin, 1/2 tsp cayenne pepper, tsp of dried thyme, tsp of basil. I used cabernet sauvignon for the wine.  I cut down on adding any salt as additions above have plenty. I also seared the beef (sirloin was so tender, I avoid stew beef, too tough) in garlic and red pepper. Cooked on high for 1.5 hrs, turned down to low for about an hour and then back to high. Took 6hrs to cook. I also added dumplings during the last 25 mins. Best stew I have ever made, but a bit salty. Used low sodium beef broth and two tsp of tomato paste as well.

text:
I'm really leaning toward 5 stars on this, but it's not OMG! good, and my husband rated it a 3.5 because he thinks it's missing something...  Anyway, this IS very good.  Simple, straight-forward comfort food.  The preparation did take almost an hour, though.  Used chuck roast cut into large cubes for the stew meat.  Doubled or tripled the veggies (large chop celery, carrots) - definitely a good change.  I used about a cup of Malbec and a can of beef broth in place of the water.  Did not sautee the onions.  Added a few cloves of minced garlic.  Cooked on high 4 hours.  Did not need to thicken in the end.  Overall very good; would definitely make again.  Next time, less (or a tamer) wine, maybe sautee the onions for flavor only, and add peas at the end.  Makes about 8 servings.

I am going to make it again for a big family dinner this weekend and instead of adding potatoes in the stew, I am going to make mashed potatoes to accompany it.  I read quite a few other reviews and agree that its missing veggies. I am going to add a can of peas and a can of corn to the dish I make this weekend to hearty it up a bit.  Also, I didn't need to thicken the sauce, it was already very thick and that would've turned it into a paste. That was the only thing I did differently than the recipe.

Very delicious stew recipe! After reading reviews I didn't use the onion soup mix, just minced onion. I also used beef broth rather than water. It was way too salty though, so next time I will use half water half broth and NO salt. It was still had very good flavor though. I also didn't brown the meat before hand either. I just put it in the bottom of the crock pot and it cooked all day for about 8 hours while I was at work and the meat was perfect, very tender.

text:
I tweaked a bit and the family thought it was great: Cut/trim beef cubes-shake in bag with flour/salt. saute beef in olive oil; put beef in slow cooker then saute onions, red wine, progresso french onion soup; put cut potatoes, carrots and soup, etc. in slow cooker on high for 30 min - then low for 9 hours. 1/2 hour before, add mushrooms and stir.  when done-keep on warm and combine 12 oz sour cream with a 1/4 cup flour/cold water then pour in and stir.  Cook broad noodles, when done, add 1/2 stick butter. Serve stroganoff over buttered noodles.

text:
This was a real hit in my house!  My family isn't big on so much onion, so I did make a few tweaks for our tastes.  I cut back the chopped onion to only about half an onion.  When I sauteed the onion, I added a little extra butter, 3 cloves of minced garlic and 8 ounces of fresh sliced mushrooms, and simmered this all in the wine a bit before adding it to the crockpot.  As others mentioned, I also added an extra cup of carrots, and used 2 cups of wine and 1 cup of water with the onion soup mix - this gave me just the right amount of liquid.  My family devoured this with hot buttered rolls, and can't wait to take out the leftovers tonight!

text:
THis is a very good stew recipe. However, for 3 pounds of beef, which is a lot of meat, I added a lot more vegetables. I cut up 3 x-large carrots, 3 lbs of small, baby red potatoes, 3 large vidalia onions. I also added an extra cup of water, worsteshire sauce, tomato paste and thyme. I didn't use rosemary, but that would probably be a good addition also. There was so much, I couldn't use my slow cooker, so I put it in my large roasting pan (which holds at least a 20lb turkey) and cooked it in the oven at 300 degrees for 2 hours, and turned the heat down to 250 for 1 hour. I froze the leftovers and will have stew for quite a long time.

text:
Great hearty stew, just what I was craving for when the cool rainy nights returned. It wouldn't fit in my crock pot so I simmered it in a stock pot for about 6 hours. I added 2 cups cut beans, 3 cloves of minced garlic, worcestershire sauce, and about 1/4 cup catsup for the body and sweetening it offered. I ended up using about 1/2 cup of wine and 1/2 cup of water to deglaze the pan, then added water to the pot until it was about 1" over the contents. The idea of using a paste of warm wine and flour to thicken was great. Topped with dumplings. My family loved this.

text:
Let me preface this by saying I grew up eating inedible beef stew (the meat was so tough, you literally couldn't chew it).  So, every time I attempt beef stew, I expect the worst.  This time, I got the best.  I had some beef sirloin in my freezer from "who knows when?" which I thawed and cut into very small pieces (I have a toddler who was going to eat this).  I also diced rather than cubed the potatoes.  The carrots were frozen cut carrots.  I cut the recipe in half because I have a smaller crockpot.  I *may* have forgotten to half the black pepper, but I don't think so - it was a little much - I liked it, but my son thought it was too spicy.  The beef was ridiculously tender, the potatoes and carrots were wonderfully soft, and though the sauce came out a little lumpy looking (from the original flour, I think because the flour at the end I made sure to stir like crazy before adding) and so it was an ugly stew, but who cares - it tasted GREAT.

text:
As I am wont to do, I used this recipe as a starting point ( and it's a very good staring point, IMHO) and then "customized".   I used 1 1/4 lbs. cubed stew beef, 2 potatoes, and 2 onions, omitted the onion soup mix (didn't have any on hand) and used 3 cups of beef broth in lieu of the called-for beef bullion and water.  I added a stalk of chopped celery, rosemary, sage,  thyme, minced garlic, 1 tsp. white pepper, 1 tsp Worcestershire sauce, onion powder, a scant bit of red pepper flakes, and threw in some frozen peas in the last 15 minutes of cooking time.  I served it over Jasmine rice and both my wife and I thought it was delicious! [ We laughed, we cried, we did the dishes.]

region:

country:
None
text:
I'll give this a 4 star recipe because I tweaked it a little bit. What i did differently was that i put the beef in a ziploc bag along with the salt, 1 clove of minced garlic, about a tablespoon of  Worcestershire sauce without the flour because it sticks to the pan and you'd have to either wash it off after, or get another pan. I added more veggies as suggested (celery and mushrooms). Then when i sauted the onion in butter, i waited till it started to turn translucent then i added the 1/4 cup flour. I used 3/4 cup of frontera cabernet sauvignon merlot red wine to the skillet and this makes for an easy clean up and you can proper coat the onions with the flour. I melted two bouillon cubes in 1.5 cup warm water (as a stock substitute) and mixed it with the onion soup mix. After i transferred it all to the slow cooker, i added thyme, rosemary, along with the other spices as indicated. I added a dash of baron west indian hot sauce for a little bit of kick. Added 3 more garlic cloves, 1 more tablespoon on Worcestershire sauce. 1 hr on high and then 5 hrs on low. The last 30 mins i chopped scallions into the slow cooker while it was still watery. The final 15 mins before i put off the slow cooker i dissolved 2 tablespoons of cornstarch in a tiny bit of water and added it to make a thick stew. I had a few friends over and they all had seconds!

This is a staple for the colder weather months. I make enough to last about two meals for three people.

My twist on this recipe is to cook it over night on low (6 to 8 hrs) and then let it cool for about 30 to 60 minutes before putting it into the fridge.  Then when I get home from work, I warm it back up again. There's something about letting stews/soups/spaghetti/chilli cool off and warmed up again that makes it amazing.

text:
The recipe by itself was a bit bland but with the adjustments it came out delicious. I added probably another cup of baby carrots to the pot. When browning the meat, I added a touch of garlic powder. I also used 3 cloves of garlic, minced it and added it after the onions were removed from the skillet and put into the pan. Instead of dry parsley, I generously used fresh parsley, fresh rosemary, and fresh thyme to taste. This was key. 

I followed another reviewers suggestion for the "thickening" paste at the end and used 1/8 cup warm water and an 1/8 cup wine to mix with the flour. It gave the stew just enough kick that was really needed. 

I also salted it a bit at the end to get the end result I wanted. It was amazing! My husband kept raving about it. Served with hot French bread and butter, yum. Thank you, this will definitely be a fall favorite!

text:
I've made this stew several times now, tweaking it a little as I've learned what to expect. As written, the recipe is very good, and the gravy has a nice not-too-thick, not-too-thin consistency.  The aroma it creates while simmering is fabulous! However, my family found the flavor a bit bland.  I've taken the advice of some of the other reviewers, adding beef bullion to the water/onion soup mixture and adding garlic and thyme.  I've also added a little salt and more wine (whatever dry red wine I've had on hand).  The most recent time I made this stew I added a can of petite diced tomatoes and four fresh zuchinni squash, cubed, toward the end of the cooking process - maybe an hour before taking it up, which gave the dish a boost in flavor and texture.  I'll continue to make small alterations, but I will definately use this recipe as a starting point for stew from now on.

text:
So i loved making this recipe. I actually changed a thing or 2 in it and i loved the changes. to make it slightly healthier and not as bulky by adding potatoes, i add cooked barley. i wait till it has about 15 minutes left then add the cooked barley so it absorbs some of the flavor without sucking up all of the juice. I also love to add canned corn and green beans near the end as well to increase the amount of veggies. Also what i found my family likes more is instead of using the large chunks of beef, i get the lean bites. follow the same steps and they love the smaller pieces. to make it beefier, i add that concentrated beef stock to the package of onion soup mix. adds great flavor. thanks for the recipe!

text:
Stew came out excellent!  Hubby is on the second helping.  I did adjust the recipe a little.  After frying meat i added 4 cloves of garlic and scraped up the brown drippings and added to the crockpot.  I added 5 stalks of celery, 2 jars of pearl onions, 1 tsp. Kitchen Bouquet browning sauce, 2 bayleaves, 1/4 tsp chili powder,1 tsp. garlic powder/onion powder and 2 cans of low sodium beef broth and 1 cup of red cooking wine and 1 tsp. worcestershire sauce.  I only cooked 30 min high and 5 hrs on low setting.  During the last 30 min of cooking i added a splash of balsamic vinegar, mixed 1/2 cup of warm water and 4tbsp of cornstarch to thicken sauce. Delicious!

This recipe was a great start to play with and make my own.  My husband is a picky eater and tough critic but he raved about this more than anything I've made in a while.
I followed the recipe for the most part but used pinot grigio in place of the red wine, still using it to deglaze the pan after cooking the beef and the onions beforehand.  I also added fresh green beans and mushrooms, some garlic powder and an extra cup of water before leaving the stew to slow-cook on low for 8hrs.  When I got home, I added the flour and water and boiled some egg noodles and it was a perfect meal.
It came our really great and I will absolutely make beef stew this way from now on.  It took a while to prep in the morning but it was worth it.

text:
I decided to make this stew for my boyfriend and I late the other night so we could wake up and have stew for lunch.  I prepared the recipe almost exactly as it says, except I forgot to boil the water before adding it to the pot.  Wow, this was a HUGE mistake.  I cooked the stew on high for an hour and then switched it to low and went to sleep.  I accidentally cooked the stew for an extra 8 hours (bc I didn't wake up to my alarm) and was expecting a soggy mess! Nope, the potatoes and the carrots weren't even close to being done!  I continued to cook the stew on low and kept checking it every hour.  It took almost 12 more hours to cook this stew!!!!    The renamed "24 Hour Stew" came out pretty tasty, but wowsers did it take a long time.  The flavors were ok and it probably could have used some tomatoes.    My only advice is to boil that water before adding to the pot!  Or you will be waiting a loooong time before you get your food!

text:
Love this recipe!  Made a few changes, but everything works out fine.  I changed the meat and used a pot roast instead--found the stew meat too tough no matter how long it cooked.  I doubled the wine and marinated the pot roast in the wine, fresh garlic, and fresh thyme overnight first.  I then browned the roast and used the same pan to cook the onions in then using the marinade to deglaze the pan.  I added everything to the crock pot, and used half beef broth and water to disolve the onion soup in.  It turns out absolutely fabulous and my whole family loves it.  Oh-I threw in a bay leaf too.  Thanks much

The only difference I made was I used only half the packet of onion soup mix and then used half a packet of McCormicks Beef stew seasoning (but I think it would be fine without it). text:
This recipe turned out well, but my family and I found it to be a bit on the bland side on its own.
First off, I reduced the potatoes--I personally don't care for potatoes too much-plus, I felt that they were out of proportion to the amount of carrots.
Towards the end of cooking-(when I realized the flavor needed a little help)  I added a couple of bay leaves, extra black pepper, FRESH parsley, a dash of balsamic vinegar and it was actually pretty yummy!  I would save this as a basic recipe to dress up.

text:
This recipe had a great flavor, thanks I believe to the use of red wine. I modified it a bit by sauteeing some minced fresh garlic with the onion. I also had to thin it out a bit with the addition of some beef broth so we'd have enough gravy to sop up with rolls. No thickening needed here! Overall, the stew was a hit, with my son-in-law eating three bowls full and asking if he could take some of the leftovers to work for lunch the next day. I'll definitely make this one again on the next cold, snowy day we have...uhhh, tomorrow, I think!
